text:
Wish I could give this one more than 5 stars... These were the best turkey burgers I've yet to make! I did use 2 chipotle peppers because we like our food spicy, and they came out just right. I was afraid that using 2 of them would overpower the meat, but it did not. Now here's a GREAT tip to keeping these tasty burgers moist: instead of adding a slice of mozzarella on top, make 8 thin patties instead of 4 thick ones. Put a heaping tablespoon of finely shredded mozzarella on the center of 4 of them and then top each with the other thin patty. Then just seal up the sides of the burger. That way, when you bite into one of these yummy delights, the cheese will ooze out of the middle. Even my husband enjoyed these, (he ate 2 of them!), and he NEVER has been impressed with any type of turkey burger! Thanks for submitting this one; I'll be making it again for sure!

My husband and I have never tried turkey burgers before but this recipe sounded interesting.  I made it just the way it is written except didn't have mozzerella so I used provolone.  I served it on whole wheat buns with sliced orange tomato.  It was delicious but next time I would use another chipotle b/c we like it a little spicier.  Our burgers were not dry at all - they were perfect.  I served sliced orange and red tomatoes and sweet corn on the side and we ate outside - perfect meal for a hot and sunny day!  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
MAKE THESE BURGERS TONIGHT!!! Looking for a change of pace from tacos made with turkey meat we decided to try these burgers. All I can say is wow! It's cold here so I cooked on the electric indoor grill for about 7 minutes. Topped bun with lettuce, avocado slices (a must) and Mont Jack instead of mozzarella (personal preference). Followed others' advice and used two peppers. Just enough heat. Hubby was blown away. So impressed, these burgers will be a staple in our house. PS don't skip the cilantro, it adds a wonderful fresh taste and an extra layer of flavor.

text:
Amazing! I did add 2 peppers but I took the seeds out of them so I could still have all the smokey flavor of the peppers without the extreme heat. I also added 1/3 cup of panko bread crumbs and 1 tbsp of greek yogurt for extra moisture. I put them in the freezer for about 2 hours to firm them up and then cooked them. OMG they were so delicious I didn't even use any cheese. I did however top them with a chipotle mayo sour cream that I like. It's just 2 tbsp. fat free sour cream and 1 tbsp low fat mayo with as much chipotle pepper as you like and about 1 1/2 tsps of  the adobo sauce. Awesome with some sweet potato fries!! Can't wait to eat the extra patties that I left in the freezer.

text:
Yes! These burgers are AMAZING! I'm so grateful to have found this recipe. I'm training for a marathon, and while much of my training diet consists of healthy carbs, I've been searching high and low for some good poultry recipes to avoid the monotony of cooking yet another chicken breast. I've been reading about the benefits of dark meat poultry -- a new thing for me as I have always stayed with the white meat -- so for this recipe, I wanted to purchase half white meat and half dark meat ground turkey. Inadvertently, I ended up buying ground turkey thigh and ground chicken breast instead. Chicken. Turkey. Even beef or salmon -- it doesn't matter. This recipe (in my opinion) would be excellent with all of those! I followed another reviewer's suggestion and upped the chipotles to two. So tasty. I can't wait to make these again and share it with those I love. That is what great recipes are all about!

Always trying a new way to add some flavor to turkey burgers  and this definitely fit the bill!  This was really good!   We like a little extra spice, so, I used 2 chipotle peppers and about 1 tbsp of the adobe sauce.  I was out of seasoned salt - so I used montreal steak seasoning instead.  I topped it with a sauce made of 1/2 cup mayo, 2 tbsps sriracha hot sauce, and 1 tbsp of lime juice.  We cooked in a covered skillet on the stove top and it was moist and juicy.  Definitely will make again!

Good burger, not dry at all as some (most) turkey burgers tend to be. we like things on the spicy side in our house so we used 2 1/2 chipoltle peppers, 2 large cloves of minced garlic and a bit of cumin. Use fresh mozzarella rather than the packaged/wrapped stuff, it really is SO much better. We've served them on both fresh kaiser rolls and fresh ciabatta rolls and both we're fantastic. I love them topped with some avacado slices yum!

text:
Excellent burgers! I processed the whole can of chipotle chili in abodo sauce in my Magic Bullet and used 1 heaping T. in the meat.  You can then put the rest of chili sauce in a ziplock and freeze for next time (per Rachael Ray - just cut out a piece when you need).  I also made a chipotle mayo to go with which really kicked it up a notch (3T low fat mayo and 1 tsp chili sauce).  With the sauce on both sides, the burger had just the right heat.  Also used 2 lbs of turkey and the same amount of spices (plenty of flavor).  Also only used 1 T. of dried Cilantro and 2 T. grated onion with juice instead of chopped.  Cooked on indoor grill.  Very yummy!

text:
Sooo good.  Best turkey burger I ever had. Didn't think I'd ever like it as a staple, ya know, only a once in a great while type a deal.  I was wrong!  Love these burgers. After your coals are ready on the BBQ, brush grate, then spray with Pam.  Haven't had one stick to the grill and fall apart yet.  I use arugula, mozzarella  cheese which melts awesomely over patty, sliced tomato with kosher salt and fresh cracked pepper. The ground turkey I get is 2lbs so I double up on all ingredients adding an extra chipotle or two. Try them, you will love them too.  Make extra patty for work! They microwave up great next day

text:
Great turkey burgers! Because we like spicy food (and because so many recipes claiming to be spicy aren't always hot enough for us), I added a couple of diced SLICES of jar jalapenos and a couple of shakes of Cajun seasoning. This made it REAL, nose-running spicy! Yum! I also used 1 tsp minced garlic instead of garlic powder. I did not have chipotle chile so I used 1 tbsp chipotle chili powder instead. I didn't have fresh cilantro, so used 1 tbsp dried. Lastly, I topped with sauteed grilled onions and mushrooms, and reduced fat cheddar. Thanks!

This was delicious, I had them about two hours aog. Wow are these ever good! Instead of cilantro which I didn't have (not crazy about the stuff anyway) I very finely minced an orange bell pepper half and added that in. Also added an egg to help hold things together. After making the patties I set them on a flour dusted wax paper lined cookie sheet and into the freezer they went. They firm up in about 15 minutes and there is no problem with them breaking up on the grill. Provolone is great on these and I made a chipotle mayo to serve on top. We all loved them, lots of oohs and aaahs at the table tonight!

text:
MMMMMM, so good!  We love turkey burgers and tend to eat them way more than beef ones, so I love trying different variations.  I actually ran out of 'real onion' so threw in a 3 onion dried blend that I have and used 2 cloves of fresh garlic instead of the powder. I left out the seasoning salt and since we don't like cilantro, I added some fresh basil. Used 1 1/2 chipotle peppers (removing some of the seeds) and threw in a good sprinkling of panko breadcrumbs to help bind as some of my turkey was still a bit frozen.  We did not find these too spicy at all, would up the chipotle next time or just not take out as many seeds, but there will defintiely be a next time!

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674147.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
These burgers were pretty fantastic :)  I made a couple of adjustments:  first, I doubled the recipe and used two garlic cloves instead of garlic powder, and I threw in half of a large yellow onion.  I'm not a big fan of onion chunks in my food, so I pureed the cilantro, garlic, chipotle and onion in a blender with a tablespoon of water, then mixed it with the ground turkey and seasonings by hand.  This left me with a pretty wet consistency, but still firm enough to form into patties on some parchment paper.

I cooked the patties in some olive oil on medium-low heat on the stovetop (too hot outside to grill).  You've got to cook them at medium-low because you really want them to cook through--after all, it's poultry, not beef.

Since we're on a low-carb diet here at the house, I served them in some leaves of iceberg lettuce, with about a teaspoon of Vietnamese red chili-garlic sauce they have in the ethnic food section, topped with a little swiss cheese.  I also had some sauteed bell pepper on the side, but they really didn't add much imo.

Lots of flavor, will undoubtedly try again.

text:
I LOVED these burgers although the hubby thought they were average. Next time, I will add more chipotle peppers & adobo sauce since I didn't think they were very spicy, but oh so good! Maybe add red pepper flakes, too. Unsure what to expect (thought it would be more "mexican" but it wasn't, but not disappointed); The chipotle in adobo added sweet and smoky flavor. I used 85/15 lean turkey and used just a quarter piece of pepperjack cheese in the middle (as suggested) which kept them very juicy. Served with just tomato, lettuce, and mustard b/c unsure how to dress at first. yum.

text:
It was really good. I used about 5 tablespoons cilantro and would use even more next time. They didn't have the chipotle chili's at my local grocery stores so I used jalapenos and Adobo Criollo sauce. It probably would have been better using the right stuff but it was still good. I served it w/ mayo but it was way better when we added ketchup and a tomato to it as well. I think it would be awesome with a spicy guacamole, I will definitely do that next time. I also put the mozzarella in between 2 small patties turning them into one large one and it was very good like that. I will use more than 1 teaspoon of cheese inside next time though. Oh yeah, I also added 1 teaspoon of cumin which was a wonderful touch. all in all, it is a very good recipe!

text:
Really, really tasty. I was worried about these being dry, but the adobo sauce must help to keep the moisture. You can use more or less of the sauce that the chiles are packed in to make it more hot. Make sure to really really dice that chipotle. I think I had a couple chunks or maybe some very sensitive eaters because I got a couple: ooooo, that's hot. I really, really like these, though. Making a habit of doubling the recipe and throwing them in the freezer separated by wax paper. Tip: Try to make them as flat as possible because the burgers have a natural tendency to kind of puck-up in the middle.

text:
Great flavor!  I have a pork and beef allergy (caused by a tick bite) and can no longer eat regular burgers.  This burger is a great replacement for the beef burgers I have missed.  It is flavorful, moist and has a texture similar to regular burgers.  The only change I made was to use one can of chipotles to 3 pounds of ground turkey.  I also used the left over adobe sauce and mixed with some mayo to make chipotle mayo and served with the burgers.  I have probably made these ten times and still really enjoy the texture and flavor--almost don't miss beef burgers anymore.  Thanks for posting this recipe!

I followed the other recommendations to up the cilantro, and add 2 chipotle peppers, and add 1 tbsp Greek yogurt and 1/4 tsp paprika.   It was very tasty.  The mozzarella detracted from the flavor of the patty, so I won't use cheese again.  I also used another's suggestion to take 2 tbsp sour cream, 1 tbsp mayo and 1.5 tsp of the chipotle sauce to use as a spicy mayo.  
I would make again.

text:
So glad I found this recipe. I find it hard to find a great recipe for ground turkey as I find it needs a lot more seasoning/flavour help than ground beef. 

I took the advice of others and upped the chipotle peppers even though I don't like spicy foods and it wasn't spicy. I use the 4 pack of ground turkey from Costco and used a full small can of the peppers (there were 7 in there) but left the sauce out. I also added more cilantro. Tossed all the seasoning ingredients into a food processor to chop and combine, then mixed that into the turkey.

I made burger patties that I froze and haven't yet tasted, then cooked the remaining meat (with no cheese) in a frying pan and put it over some salad. Tasty!

text:
I followed this recipe exactly except for 4 basic things: I used 1.5 lbs of 70% lean ground beef instead of 1 lb of turkey, 2 chipotle peppers instead of 1, 1 teaspoon of ground cinnamon instead of cilantro, and cooked the patties in a frying pan (without any cooking oil) instead of cooking them the girl. I topped them with cheese (asadero & cheddar) immediately after they were cooked and covered them in the pan so the cheese would melt. After the cheese melted, I put them on top of a paper-towelled plate to rest before placing them on toasted buns (VERY important to collect excess grease so they don't ruin the buns). Mmmm, good! They were a hit, and I have to cook for a picky 16 year-old who devoured them and said they were good. What a great recipe! Thanks. :)

This was so easy and good.  Most turkey burgers are bland, these had plenty of flavor!  I read some of the other reviews and some people suggested using two of the adobo chilies. None
text:
Add chipotle ketchup to top it off!  To make the chipotle ketchup, just take one of the left over chipotle peppers and a tablespoon or so of the adobe sauce.  Finely chop the pepper and add the sauce and pepper to 1/8th to 1/4 cup of standard ketchup.  Keep adding ketchup until you get the heat level/flavor intensity you like.  Then serve with the burgers.  

PS.  I personally use 4 chipotle peppers per pound of turkey for this recipe - nice heat at this level, but not too overpowering for those who like hot foods.

country:
None
text:
This was one of the most flavorful turkey burgers that I have ever tasted. I wanted to try this recipe because a) I love spicy food, b) the ingredients were simple and things I already had on hand. I did tweak the recipe a little based on my personal preferences and comments that other reviewers made.

1st: Turkey burgers tend to suffer from dryness and I didn't want that, so what I did was saute the 1/2 cup of chopped onions in 2 tbsp of EVOO. I let it cool slightly and then added it to the meat.

2nd: I added 1 tsp of ranch powder (because ranch makes everything better in my opinion :-) I also added 1 finely chopped roasted red pepper because I felt that this would compliment the flavor profile of the recipe.

3rd: Some reviewers suggested adding 1 extra chipotle pepper for more spice and some cumin. I did both of these things, however I only added 1/2 tsp of cumin because I didn't want it to overwhelm the turkey.

I put this in the fridge to let the flavors combine and then cooked them on the charcoal grill. What resulted was a juicy, flavorful, spicy turkey burger. I used pepper jack cheese for extra bite. (If you aren't prone to spicy foods, I think that 1 chipotle pepper will do the trick). Try and enjoy this recipe, you will not regret it.

Had to make a few changes...

The grocery store was almost out of ground turkey, so I mixed turkey with ground chicken.

I used Italian Parsley instead of cilantro, and didn't use the chipotle chili...  I wasn't sure how hot they are and didn't want to overdo it, plus I didn't really want to buy a jar of them to only use a single pepper... so instead I poured in a couple tablespoons of Franks Red Hot Buffalo Chicken sauce.  I know,  completely different taste that what the pepper would have provided, but that's what I did. :p

End result... fantastic!  Great combo of spice in the burgers, nice and moist.

Will definitely make these again, they were so easy to make and delicious.

text:
I fixed these burgers for a cookout I hosted last Friday. I couldn't get my outdoor grill fire going to  medium high, I was working with a charcol grill,  so it was a slow cook time that more or less smoked the burgers. THEY TURNED OUT AMAZING! EVERYONE WENT CRAZY about the burgers! I also put the mozorella cheese inside and it was an unexpected treat. 

They were such a hit I had to make another batch of them with 4lbs of turkey on Sunday. I did the second batch on my indoor grill. They turned out great. Just watch the chesse, you dont want it seeping out the sides. I suggest when making the patty make a well and insert the cheese then roll the patty into a ball and loosley flatten - indoor grills will continue to flatten the patty out. 

I loved the flavors and the chesse complimented the spices well. I did add an extra pepper per pound. 

An excellent recipe my friends and family can't wait for me to make again. I will say that to get decent size burgers it's best to stick to 4-5 burgers per pound. Trying to make more that number causes the patties to look like little turkey rocks Lol! 

Will post pictures if I can keep hands off long enough to get the camera!!

I had all intentions of making the recipe just as written, then got lazy.  So I give it 5 stars because I only used the dried spices, oiled the patties before grilling and called it done.
